	HNV 369.  AmaH kR-bhv-astayo `nuprayujyante | the dhAtus [Du]kR[J], bhU, or as[a] are added after Am |
when the dhAtus [Du]kR[J], bhU, and as[a] are applied after Am, they are merely auxiliary verbs, and thus they do not alter the meaning of the dhAtu to which Am is applied |

	HNV 1276:  abhUta-tad-bhAve kR-bhv-asti-yoge viH, kRJi karmani bhv-astyoH kartari - vi is applied in connection with kR, bhU, and as in the sense of becoming that which it was not before | in that regard, vi is applied after the karma when used in connection with kR but after the kartA when used in connection with bhU and as |
	vRtti - all the letters of the pratyaya vi are indicatory letters.
	amRta - the statement viH sarva it was made keeping in mind the rule kevalasya pratyaya ver haraH (HNV 612) |
	saMzodhinI  (from HNV 1277) - one should remember that vi is also used in conjuction with kRdanta forms of kR, bhU, and as by upendrory-Adi-vy-antAj-anta-pUrva-padAni kRdantena samasyante (HNV 776) |

	HNV 1278:  sAtir vA vi-viSaye kArtsnye - sAt[i] is optionally applied instead of vi when something changes entirely | bhasmasAt-syAt kaluSaH "the sin completety becomes ashes" |

*[ikh]{a} gatau

*[ikh]{i} gatau
1P, seT, sak
to go, move

	HNV 368.  Rccha-varjita-gurv-IzvarAder Am adhokSaje | Am is applied after any dhAtu, except Rcch[a], which begins with an Izvara that is guru when an adhokSaja pratyaya follows |
	as was explained in vRtti 344, when dhAtus that have the indicatory letter i take n[um] by i-rAmed-dhAtor num (344), the n[um] is considered original (upadeza). and since when n[um] is applied a sat-saGga is formed, the initial Izvara of dhAtus which have the indicatory letter i is also guru. thus the this dhAtus follows this rule |

	laT 1.1 [ekhati] - BDK

	HNV 368.  Rccha-varjita-gurv-IzvarAder Am adhokSaje | Am is applied after any dhAtu, except Rcch[a], which begins with an Izvara that is guru when an adhokSaja pratyaya follows |
	as was explained in vRtti 344, when dhAtus that have the indicatory letter i take n[um] by i-rAmed-dhAtor num (344), the n[um] is considered original (upadeza). and since when n[um] is applied a sat-saGga is formed, the initial Izvara of dhAtus which have the indicatory letter i is also guru. thus the this dhAtus follows this rule |

		liT pa. | HNV |

	2.1 [uvokhitha] 2.2 [UkhathuH] 2.3 [Ukha]
	3.1 [uvokha] 3.2 [Ukhiva] 3.3 [Ukhima]

	as was explained in vRtti 344, when dhAtus that have the indicatory letter i take n[um] by i-rAmed-dhAtor num (344), the n[um] is considered original (upadeza). and since when n[um] is applied a sat-saGga is formed, the initial Izvara of dhAtus which have the indicatory letter i is also guru. thus the this dhAtus follows this rule |

*[kaS]{a} hiMsAyAm
1P, seT, sak
to hurt, kill

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

	HNV 356.  kR-sR-bhR-vR-stu-dru-sru-zrubhya evAdhokSaja-mAtre neT, anyebhyas tv aniDbhyo `pIT | when an adhokSaja pratyaya follows this dhAtu doesn`t take i[T] | all other dhAtus take i[T], even if they are aniT.

{Du}*[kR]{J} karaNe
8U, aniT, sak
to do, make

	HNV 356.  kR-sR-bhR-vR-stu-dru-sru-zrubhya evAdhokSaja-mAtre neT, anyebhyas tv aniDbhyo `pIT | when an adhokSaja pratyaya follows this dhAtu doesn`t take i[T] | all other dhAtus take i[T], even if they are aniT.

	HNV 369.  AmaH kR-bhv-astayo `nuprayujyante | the dhAtus [Du]kR[J], bhU, or as[a] are added after Am |
when the dhAtus [Du]kR[J], bhU, and as[a] are applied after Am, they are merely auxiliary verbs, and thus they do not alter the meaning of the dhAtu to which Am is applied |

	HNV 370.  kRJa Am-anta-dhAtu-vat parapadAdi | in kartari prayoga, the dhAtu [Du]kR[J] takes the parapada endings and so on according to the dhAtu ending in Am |
	this rule is given to prevent [Du]kR[J] from functioning as an ubhayapadI dhAtu when it comes after a dhAtu ending in Am. thus, when the dhAtu ending in Am is AtmapadI, [Du]kR[J] takes the Atmapada endings, and when the dhAtu ending in Am is parapadI, [Du]kR[J] takes the parapada endings (and when the dhAtu ending in Am is ubhayapadI, [Du]kR[J] can take the parapada endings or the Atmapada endings) |

	HNV 1276:  abhUta-tad-bhAve kR-bhv-asti-yoge viH, kRJi karmani bhv-astyoH kartari - vi is applied in connection with kR, bhU, and as in the sense of becoming that which it was not before | in that regard, vi is applied after the karma when used in connection with kR but after the kartA when used in connection with bhU and as |
	vRtti - all the letters of the pratyaya vi are indicatory letters.
	amRta - the statement viH sarva it was made keeping in mind the rule kevalasya pratyaya ver haraH (HNV 612) |
	saMzodhinI  (from HNV 1277) - one should remember that vi is also used in conjuction with kRdanta forms of kR, bhU, and as by upendrory-Adi-vy-antAj-anta-pUrva-padAni kRdantena samasyante (HNV 776) |

	HNV 1278:  sAtir vA vi-viSaye kArtsnye - sAt[i] is optionally applied instead of vi when something changes entirely | thus we get pApaM bhasmasAt-karoti viSNu-bhaktiH or pApaM bhasmI-karoti viSNu-bhaktiH "devotion to viSNu completely turns sin into ashes" |

*[kRv]{i} hiMsAyAm
1P, seT, sak
to hurt, kill

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

*[kSaN]{u} hiMsAyAm
8U, seT, sak
to hurt, kill

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

*[kSi] nivAsa-gatyoH
6P, aniT, sak
to dwell; to go, move

*[kSiN]{u} hiMsAyAm
8U, seT, sak
to hurt, kill

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

        adhi: accomplish, acquire, approach, learn, marry |
        abhi: approach, visit, find, meet with, cohabit
        A: gajaH Agacchati the elephant comes |
        ud: dhUliH udgacchati the dust rises up |
        prati + ud: janakaH vizvAmitraM pratyudgacchati janaka greets vizvAmitra |

	HNV 355.  R-dvayAd viSNujanAntezoddhavAc ca vaiSNavAdi-si-kAmapAlau kapilAv Atmapade, games tu vA | when an Atmapada pratyaya comes after a dhAtu ending in R-dvaya or after a dhAtu that ends in a viSNujana and has an Iza as its uddhava, s[i] and kAmapAla which begin with a vaiSNava are kapila | but when an Atmapada pratyaya comes after gam[L], s[i] and kAmapAla which begin with a vaiSNava are optionally kapila |

	N.B. among the ghaT-Adis, this dhAtu is understood as having the indicatory letter {S} | the result of these dhAtus having the indicatory letter {S} is that {G}A{p} will be applied instead of {k}ti in accordance with the sUtra Sid-bhid-Adibhyaz ca (HNV 905) | thus we will get ghaTA, vyathA, and so on |

*[cakAs]{R} dIptau

*[cakS]{iG} vyaktAyAM vAci
2A, seT, sak
to speak, say, tell

	N.B. amRta - the dhAtu cakS{iG} is always preceded by A{G} when the meaning is vyaktAyAM vAci "to speak, say, tell", but not when the meaning is something else | thus vyacakSata "he saw" (laG At. 1.3 of vi + cakS{iG} vyaktAyAM vAci) and samacakSiSTa "he excluded" (luG At. 1.1 of sam + cakS{iG} vyaktAyAM vAci) |
	saMzodhinI - although the dhAtu cakS{iG} has the indicatory letter "i", it doesn't take n{um} by i-rAmed-dhAtor num (344) because the i is not kevala since it is accompanied by "G" (see AmRta 440) | moreover, by saying "the i is for the sake of pronunciation (uccAraNa), jIva gosvAmI blocks the insertion of n{um} in another way, because if an indicatory letter is used to aid pronunciation (uccArANa) it cannot also be the cause of a rule or prohibition (vidhy-Adi-nimitta) | furthermore, although the dhAtu cakS{iG} is listed in the dhATu-pATha as meaning vyaktAyAM vAci "to speak, say, tell", it is frequently used in the meaning of darzana "to see" , and when it has this meaning it is not preceded by A{G} | thus, in his commentary on the bhAg. entitled bhAvArtha-dIpikA, zrIdhara svAmI glosses acaSTa (laG At. 1.1 of cakS{iG} vyaktAyAm vAci) in bhAg. 4.9.8 as apazyat "he saw" and acakSata (laG At. 1.3 of cakS{iG} vyaktAyAm vAci) in bhAg. 3.2.24 as apazyan "they saw" | therefore whenever the dhAtu cakS{iG} isn't preceded by A{G} it means "to see," but when it is preceded by A{G} it means "to speak, say, tell |"

	HNV 365.  jRR-bhramu-trasa-phaNAdInAM hiMsArtha-rAdhaz ca vA | the medial vowel of this dhAtu also optionally changes to e when a kapila adhokSaja pratyaya or tha[l] with i[T] follows, and after that his nara disappears |

*[jJap]{a} (jJAna-jJApana-)mAraNAdau
10P, seT, sak (ghaT-Adi)
to know; to inform; to kill; to satisfy; to sharpen

	N.B. one of the main commentators on the pANinian dhATu-pATha, lists this dhAtu as jJap{a} mAraNa-toSaNa-nizAmaneSu mic ca  (10P, "to kill; to satisfy; to sharpen" and gives the following examples for each meaning: pazuM saMjJapayati "he kills the sacrificial animal", viSNuM vijJapayati "he satisfies viSNu", and zastraM prajJapayati "he sharpens the weapon". however, this dhAtu is often just listed as jJap{a} mic ca, and the meaning is supplied by the commentator. in this regard, siddhAnta kaumudI, commenting on mAraNa-toSaNa-nizAmaneSu jJA, says jJapa mic ca iti cur-Adau, jJApanaM mAraNAdikaM ca tasyArthaH "among the cur-Adi-dhAtus is jJap{a} mic ca | its meanings are jJApana and mAraNa and so on", and, commenting on the cur-Adi-dhAtu jJap{a} mic ca, it says ayam jJAne jJApane ca vartate "this dhAtu is used in the sense of jJAna and jJApana" | this last statement of siddhAnta kaumudI is an observation based upon how pANini himself has used the dhAtu | for example, in the dhATu-pATha, pANini says pracch{a} jJIpsAyAm "the dhAtu pracch{a} (6p) is used in the sense of jJIpsA  "inquiry, desire to know"" | here the meaning of jJap{a} is jJAna "knowing" | but in zlAgha-hnuG-sthA-zapAM jJIpsyamAnaH  (aSTAdhyAyI 1.4.34) the meaning of jJap{a} is jJApana "informing, causing to know" | therefore, considering all these opinions, the bRhad-dhAtu-kusumAkara lists this dhAtu as jJap{a} jJAna-jJApana-mAraNa-toSaNa-nizAmaneSu (10p, "to know; to inform; to kill; to satisfy; to sharpen" | in the edition of HNV of Matsya Avatara dAsa therefore this dhAtu is listed as jJap{a} (jJAna-jJApana-)mAraNAdau (10p, "to know; to inform; to kill; to satisfy; to sharpen" |

		--- kRtsu ---
	[Dayitum]

--- Dha ---

*[Dhauk]{R} gatau
1A, seT, sak
to go, move

--- Na ---

*[NaT]{a} nRtau (nRtir nartanam)
1P, seT, ak (ghaT-Adi)
to dance, mime (nRti means nartana "dancing, acting")

	N.B. according to siddhAnta-kaumudI, this dhAtu is a Nopadeza dhAtu | some list the meaning natau "to bow" instead of nRtau | others list the meaning as gatau "to go, move" |

*[Nad]{a} avyakte zabde
1P, seT, ak
to sound, roar

*[Nad]{a} dIptau
10P, seT, ak
to shine

*[Nam]{a} prahvatve zabde ca (prahvatvaM namaskAro namratA ca)
1P, seT, sak, ak (ghaT-Adi vA (when it doesn't come after an upendra))
to bend, bow down; to sound (prahvatva means namaskAra "offering obeisances" and namratA "being submissive")

	N.B. Nam{a} is a ghaT-Adi by the phrase am-antAz ca, but gaNa-sUtra limits that by saying that it is only optionally ghaT-Adi when it desn't come after an upendra | but siddhAnta-kaumudI confirms that it is always ghaT-Adi when it does come after an upendra |

        ktavatu: [natavAn]

*[tUr]{I} tvaraNa-hiMsayoH
4A, seT, sak
to make haste; to hurt, kill

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

*[dam]{u} upazame
4P, seT, sak (puS-Adi, zam-Adi, ghaT-Adi)
to tame, subdue

	N.B. commenting on this dhAtu, siddhAnta-kaumudI says upazama ity Ny-antasya | tena sakarmako 'yam, na tu zami-vad akarmakaH "the word upazama in dam{u} upazame is made from a Ny-anta-dhAtu | thus dam{u} is sakarmaka, unlike zam{u} which is akarmaka" | the word upazama in dam{u} upazame is made from upa + zam{u} + {N}i + {gh}a{N} and there is no vRSNIndra because of HNV sUtra 397 | thus the sense is cause to be calm" or, in other words, tame, subdue |" this upazama is different from the upazama in zam{u} upazame which is formed from upa + zam{u} + {gh}a{N} and which just means be calm |"

*[pij]{i} hiMsAyAm
10P, seT, sak
to hurt, kill

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but [ghAtayati] "he kills" also |

*[bhuj]{a} pAlanAbhyavahArayoH
7P, aniT, sak
to protect, rule; to eat, enjoy

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI lists this dhAtu as a parapadI, but it also takes At. endings in accordance with anavane bhunakteH | thus it is parapadI when it is used in the sense of pAlana "protecting, ruling", but when it is used in any other sense, it is AtmapadI |

*[bhuj]{o} kauTilye
6P, aniT, ak
to bend, curve, be crooked

*[bhU] avakalpane
10P, seT, sak
to consider, think of, meditate

	N.B. in the pANinian dhATu-pATha this dhAtu is listed as bhuvo 'vakalpane and kRp{a} avakalpane is listed as kRpez ca | in both cases the sixth case singular is used and, in the case of kRpeH, i{k} is used | commenting on the meaning of avakalpana here, siddhAnta-kaumudI says avakalpanaM mizrI-karaNam ity eke, cintanam ity anye "some say avakalpana means mizrI-karaNa "to mix" | others say avakalpana means cintana "to think, consider, meditate"" | the meaning of cintana, however, is the commonly accepted meaning | for example, in prayuktAkyAta-maJjarI rUpa gosvAmI says dhyAne cintayati dhyAyaty AmI bhAvayati trayam "these three, i.e cintayati, dhyAyati, and bhAvayati, are used in the sense of dhyAna "meditation, consideration"" | similarly, in vizvanAtha cakravartI's gurv-aSTaka we have sAkSAd-dharitvena samasta-zAstrair uktas tathA bhAvyata eva sadbhiH "the guru is said by all the scriptures to be directly hari, and he is considered in the same way by the saintly persons" |

*[bhU] prAptau (aNy-antas tUbhayapadI)
10A, seT, sak (yuj-Adi)
to obtain

	this dhAtu is listed as a AtmapadI dhAtu, but jIva gosvAmI adds the comment aNy-antas tUbhayapadI "but when it doesn’t take [N]i, it is ubhayapadI" | thus dhAtu has three acyuta 1.1 forms: [bhAvayate], [bhavati], and [bhavate] |

*[bhU] sattAyAm
1P, seT, ak
to be, become, exist

	HNV 369.  AmaH kR-bhv-astayo `nuprayujyante | the dhAtus [Du]kR[J], bhU, or as[a] are added after Am |
when the dhAtus [Du]kR[J], bhU, and as[a] are applied after Am, they are merely auxiliary verbs, and thus they do not alter the meaning of the dhAtu to which Am is applied |

	HNV 1276:  abhUta-tad-bhAve kR-bhv-asti-yoge viH, kRJi karmani bhv-astyoH kartari - "vi" is applied in connection with "kR", "bhU", and "as" in the sense of becoming that which it was not before | in that regard, "vi" is applied after the karma when used in connection with "kR" but after the kartA when used in connection with "bhU" and "as" |
	vRtti - all the letters of the pratyaya "vi" are indicatory letters |
	amRta - the statement viH sarva it was made keeping in mind the rule kevalasya pratyaya ver haraH (HNV 612) |
	saMzodhinI  (from HNV 1277) - one should remember that "vi" is also used in conjuction with kRdanta forms of "kR", "bhU", and "as" by upendrory-Adi-vy-antAj-anta-pUrva-padAni kRdantena samasyante (HNV 776) |

	HNV 1278:  sAtir vA vi-viSaye kArtsnye - sAt[i] is optionally applied instead of "vi" when something changes entirely | bhasmasAd-bhavati kaluSaH "the sin completety becomes ashes" |

*[mI]{G} hiMsAyAm
4A, aniT, sak
to harm, kill

	N.B. this dhAtu is understood as having an indicatory o-rAma in accordance with the sv-AdayaH o-rAmetaH | the dhAtus from SU{G} to vrI{G} are understood as having an indicatory o-rAma |
	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

*[mrad]{a} mardane 
1A, seT, sak (ghaT-Adi)
to crush

	N.B. among the ghaT-Adis, this dhAtu is understood as having the indicatory letter {S} | the result of these dhAtus having the indicatory letter {S} is that {G}A{p} will be applied instead of {k}ti in accordance with the sUtra Sid-bhid-Adibhyaz ca (HNV 905) | thus we will get ghaTA, vyathA, and so on |

*[radh]{a} saMrAddhau hiMsAyAM ca
4P, veT, sak (puS-Adi, radh-Adi)
to accomplish, be completed; to hurt, kill

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

	HNV 365.  jRR-bhramu-trasa-phaNAdInAM hiMsArtha-rAdhaz ca vA | the medial vowel of this dhAtu also optionally changes to e when a kapila adhokSaja pratyaya or tha[l] with i[T] follows, and after that his nara disappears |

*[rAdh]{a} saMsiddhau
4P, aniT, sak
to succeed, accomplish

	HNV 365.  jRR-bhramu-trasa-phaNAdInAM hiMsArtha-rAdhaz ca vA | the medial vowel of this dhAtu [with upasarga apa] also optionally changes to e when a kapila adhokSaja pratyaya or tha[l] with i[T] follows, and after that his nara disappears | (as was explained in amRta 301, upasargas merely bring out the various meanings that are inherent within the dhAtus themselves. here the upasarga apa brings out the inherent meaning of hiMsA within the dhAtu rAdh[a] saMsiddhau. otherwise, when used by itself, the dhAtu rAdh[a] saMsiddhau doesn`t have the meaning of hiMsA, but only that of saMsiddhi.)

		--- upasargas ---
	apa: to offend

		--- upasargas ---
	apa: to offend

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

*[rI] gatau reSaNe ca (reSaNaM vRka-dhvaniH)

*[vyac]{a} vyAjI-karaNe

*[vyath]{a} bhaye duHkhe calane ca
1A, seT, ak (ghaT-Adi)
to be unhappy; to be afraid; to tremble

	N.B. among the ghaT-Adis, this dhAtu is understood as having the indicatory letter {S} | the result of these dhAtus having the indicatory letter {S} is that {G}A{p} will be applied instead of {k}ti in accordance with the sUtra Sid-bhid-Adibhyaz ca (HNV 905) | thus we will get ghaTA, vyathA, and so on |

*[zabd]{a} upendra-pUrva AviSkAre
10P, seT, sak
this dhAtu is preceded by an upendra and it means reveal |

	N.B. in the pANinian dhATu-pATha this dhAtu is listed as zabd{a} upasargAd AviSkAre ca and siddhAnta-kaumudI says that the word ca drags in the word bhASaNe from the previous dhAtu bukk{a} bhASane (10P, bark, to speak, to sound in general" such that zabd{a} by itself is used in the sense of bhASaNa whereas zabd{a} that comes after an upasarga is used in the sense of AviSkara | however, siddhAnta-kaumudI also offers an alternate explanation of the word ca-anupasargAc ca AviSkAre ity eva "zabd{a} is also just used in the sense of AviSkAra, even when it doesn't come after an upasarga" | thus the word ca is used in the sense of upasargAd anupasargAc ca | in this way siddhAnta-kaumudI establishes that zabd{a} is also used without an upendra | similarly, AmRta explains that the form zabdanaH in vRtti 869 is made from the cur-Adi-dhAtu zabd{a} vizabdane | vizabdana is basically an equivalent of AviSkAra since jIva gosvAmI, commenting on the cur-Adi-dhAtu ghuS{ir} vizabdane, explains that vizabdana means svAbhimatAviSkaraNa "revealing one's opinion" | bAla, however, explains that the form zabdanaH in vRtti 869 is made from the cur-Adi-dhAtu zabd{a} zabda-kriyAyAm where zabda-kriyA means make a sound | but the problem is that neither zabd{a} vizabdane nor zabd{a} zabda-kriyAyAm are listed in the pANinian dhATu-pATha or in jIva gosvAmI's dhATu-pATha | thus, to make forms like zabdayati sounds" (laT pa. 1.1) and zabdanaH "one who sounds" (1.1), we either have to resort to siddhAnta-kaumudI's first explanation or we have to understand that such forms are made from the Ny-anta-dhAtu zabdi formed by applying {N}i after zabdam (2.1) in the sense of tat karoti (see sUtra 617) | this Ny-anta-dhAtu zabdi, which means "make a sound" would be equivalent in sense to the cur-Adi-dhAtu zabd{a} zabda-kriyAyAm mentioned by BAla | another feature of the dhAtu zabd{a} is that it takes on the special meaning of "called" in karmaNi prayoga | for example, zrIdhara svAmI, commenting on brahmeti paramAtmeti bhagavAn iti zabdyate (bhAg. 1.2.11), glosses zabdyate as abhidhIyate "called" | similarly we get sattvaM vizuddhaM vasudeva-zabditam "pure consciousness is called vasudeva" (bhAg. 4.3.23) |

*[zam]{u} upazame
4P, seT, sak (ghaT-Adi, puS-Adi, zam-Adi)
to be calm, peaceful (see N.B.)

	N.B. when this dhAtu is preceded by upendra ni its meaning changes to "to hear, listen" | zrIla rUpa gosvAmI in his prayuktAkhyAta-maJjarI 1.2.29 gives an example of this: zRNoty AkarNayati ca tadvan nizamayaty api nizAmyatIti zravaNe (zRNoti, AkarNayati, nizamayati, and nizAmyati mean "to hear, listen") |
	HNV 541: zam-AdInAM trivikramaH zye (the a of the zam-Adis becomes trivikrama when {z}ya follows) |
	zam + ti{p} --> (288, 537) zam + {z}ya + ti{p} --> (541) [zAmyati], laT pa. 1.1 |
	zam + ta --> (306, 313) a{t} + zam + i{N} + ta --> (397) azam + i{N} + ta --> (315) [azami], luG bhAve 1.1 |

*[zas]{u} hiMsAyAm
1P, seT, sak
to kill

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

*[ziS]{a} hiMsAyAm
1P, aniT
to hurt, kill

	N.B. this dhAtu is not listed in jIva gosvAmI's dhATu-pATha, but is listed in the pANinian dhATu-pATha |
	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

*[SUd]{a} kSaNane (kSaNanaM hiMsA)
1A, seT, sak
to hurt, kill (kSaNana means hiMsA "violence")

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

*[sRR] hiMsAyAm
9P, seT, sak (pv-Adi, lv-Adi)
to hurt, kill

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

	HNV 365.  jRR-bhramu-trasa-phaNAdInAM hiMsArtha-rAdhaz ca vA | the medial vowel of this dhAtu also optionally changes to e when a kapila adhokSaja pratyaya or tha[l] with i[T] follows, and after that his nara disappears |

*[han]{a} hiMsA-gatyoH
2P, aniT, sak
to strike, kill; to go, move

	N.B. jIva gosvAmI says hanty-arthAz ca (ye ca teSu gaNeSu hiMsArthA dhAtava uktAs te cur-AdAv api jJeyAH ity arthaH) "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also be cur-Adis (one should know that those dhAtus having the meaning of hiMsA which were previously mentioned in the other nine gaNas can also be conjugated as cur-Adis)" |
	siddhAnta-kaumudI, commenting on the same gaNa-sUtra (hanty-arthAz ca) in the pANinian dhATu-pATha, says nava-gaNyAm uktA api hanty-arthAH svArthe NicaM labhanta ity arthaH "dhAtus which mean "to kill" can also take svArtha {N}i{c} (cur-Adi-Ni) even though they are listed in the other nine gaNas" | this increases the list of cur-Adi-dhAtus considerably | thus from the ad-Adi-dhAtu han{a} hiMsA-gatyoH we can form not only hanti "he kills", but ghAtayati "he kills" also |

	520. bhI-hrI-bhR-hubhya Am adhokSaje vA, dvir-vacanaM ca | Am is optionally applied after [Ji]bhI, hrI, [Du]bhR[J], and hu when an adhokSaja pratyaya follows, and in the case that Am is inserted there is reduplication of the dhAtu ||

------------------------------------
  juhoti – 489.  na tu nArAyaNasya But when [z]a[p] undergoes mahAhara, the final u-rAma of a nArAyaNa doesn’t take vRSNIndra when a pRthu pratyaya beginning with a viSNujana follows. hu + ti[p] --> (288, 477, 519, 323) hu + hu + ti[p] --> (470) ju + hu + ti[p] --> (489, 289) juhoti |
------------------------------------
  juhoSi – 489.  na tu nArAyaNasya But when [z]a[p] undergoes mahAhara, the final u-rAma of a nArAyaNa doesn’t take vRSNIndra when a pRthu pratyaya beginning with a viSNujana follows. hu + si[p] --> (288, 477, 519, 323) hu + hu + si[p] --> (470) ju + hu + si[p] --> (489, 289) juhosi --> (108) juhoSi |
------------------------------------

		laT pa. | HNV |
	1.1 [juhoti]Ex	1.2 [juhutaH]	1.3 [juhvati]
	2.1 [juhoSi]Ex 2.2 [juhuthaH]	2.3 [juhutha]
	3.1 [juhomi]	3.2 [juhuvaH]	3.3 [juhumaH]

------------------------------------
	hu + [N]a[l] --> (two options by 520):
 		1) (Am is applied) hu + Am + [N]a[l] --> (330, 369) hu + Am + as + [N]a[l] --> (289) ho + Am + as + [N]a[l]  --> (55) hav +Am + as + [N]a[l]  --> (520, 323, the govinda o and the replacement av are sthAni-vat by 373) hu + hav + Am + as + [N]a[l]  --> (470) juhavAm + as + [N]a[l]  -->(330, 358) juhavAm + As + a --> (322, 323, the vRSNIndra A is treated like the original a by 373) juhavAm + a + As + a --> (361) juhavAm + A + As + a --> (42) juhavAmAsa <adhokSaja pa. 1.1>
		 2) (Am is not applied, 330, 314) hau + a --> (55) hAv + a --> (322, 323, the vRSNIndra au and the replacement Av are sthAni-vat by 373) hu + hAv + a --> (470) juhAva <adhokSaja pa. 1.1>
------------------------------------

*[hR]{J} haraNe (haraNaM dezAntara-prApaNam)
1U, aniT, sak
to take, remove, steal (haraNa means dezAntara-prApaNam (taking to another place))

                -- upasargas --
                
        sIta jalaM harati sIta carries water |
        pra: bhImaH duryodhanaM praharati bhIma strikes duryodhana |
        pra: vyAdhaH bANena praharati
        A: sA puNyam Aharati she brings merit |
        A: raghuH yAgam Aharati raghu performs a sacrifice |
        sam: rAmaH rAvaNaM saMharati rAma kills rAvaNa |
        vi: sarve candrikAyAM viharati all rejoce in moonlight |
        vi: rAjA antaH-pure tiSThann api cAra-caraNaH sva-rAjye viharati the king, though residing in the palace, strolls on foot in his kingdom |
        vi: kRSNaH rAdhayA saha viharati  kRSNa plays with rAdhA |
        pari: guruH saMzayaM piriharati the teacher removes the doubt |
        ut: uddharati - lifts, rescues

to sound; be happy

*[hval]{a} calane
1P, seT, ak (ghaT-Adi)
to shake, move

	N.B. usually this dhAtu would always be ghaT-Adi since hval{a} is directly listed as ghaT-Adi, but gaNa-sUtra limits that by saying that it is only optionally ghaT-Adi when it desn't come after an upendra | but siddhAnta-kaumudI confirms that it is always ghaT-Adi when it does come after an upendra |
